< Review>
So I did the research before buying a vehicle and got it down to a short list of 6-7 options. The focus was on Hyundai Santa Fe's available in CA. All of them 2018s, under $20k, and under 20k miles.

Most of them were located in SoCal but one was closer to home in Sacramento. Talked to the staff in Stockton and they had the vehicle transferred to their dealership, which saved me driving further.

Then I organised a one-way rental from a local Enterprise branch, headed up to Stockton and made the purchase. The staff were courteous, informative and helpful. Happy with the way things went and we were back on the road, in a little over an hour on our way home.

Financing went smoothly and the options were explained in detail so we able to decide on what we did and didn't need or want. I would highlight Enterprise ex-rentals to anyone looking for a late model car at a reasonable price with a good warranty package, (for Hyundais anyway).

I'd also point to doing your homework before you get to the purchasing stage of the process. I was totally stoked with our buy and wouldn't hesitate to recommend Enterprise sales as an option when buying your next car.</Review>

< review>
The Bay Club is pretty awesome, but mostly because of my trainer Matthew Ryan Carney!

If you are looking to recover from an injury, train for a specific event, or just increase your fitness, I highly recommend him. He is really great about tailoring workouts to your specific goals and needs.

He helped me recover from a hip flexor injury in time for my trip to Yosemite.  I was not getting the results I wanted from physical therapy and am so glad I found Matthew through my sister who was already training with him at Bay Club.  I went from having acute hip flexor pain and limping every time I did over 3 miles of activity to pain free after the 8.5+ miles of the ascent to Half Dome.  I really thought that I was not going to be able to summit due to my injury and was so happy that I was able to make it to the top and back down!!  If you enjoy Pilates, you should definitely go see him for some hardcore or rehabilitative reformer training!<//review>

<gmapID>0x808fb598a280ad59:0xc3581115e77b3135</gmapID><Review>Great place to workout, hangout, and work. Very spacious so I don't feel claustrophobic like other gyms that I've been too (cough, Cupertino sport center).

People here are very friendly and down to earth especially the instructors here. Here are the list of my recommendations of the classes that they offer

Tuesday: Pilates with Karen Kim

She is very knowledgeable and funny, she makes sure you have the correct form and posture, which is a PLUS because the only way to prevent sport injury and get the outcome you want is to have a great form down. Interesting side note her mom(in her 90s) can do plank for a full minute- AMAZING right ?

Thursday: Cycling with Tricia Severietti

She bring so much energy and motivation that there is no way you are going to stop paddling, always has the best playlist to cycle with

Friday: Yoga with Nick Fortino

He has a super soothing and calming voice that if you take ambien to help you sleep at night, there is no need anymore just come to his class. Very knowledgeable and informative class, again posture is BIG in yoga, and he takes time to explain using both the scientific explanation and the average Joe version to get his points across. I never really enjoy Yoga until I went to his class because I am been going to the wrong place the whole time.

Saturday: Yoga with Larry Munoz

He walks around to fix postures and form, which is a plus again especially for yoga. I think yoga needs constant fine tuning until you can get it right and Larry does a great job on assisting student to reach that point. Side track here: I think he is very handsome, look so much like George Clooney. He is the type that as he age, the more handsome he gets ( It could be from yoga - Wilde guess here )

Sunday: Athletic Conditioning with Alex Anders

There is nothing better than to burn all that bad chi out with an intense cardio session with Alex on Sunday. Here is a quick routine breakdown
1. squat jumps with resistance
2. high knees with resistance
3. side squats with resistance
4. alligator with gliders
5. TRX
6. stair masters
7. abs

-- Great employee phone skills, listening, and above/beyond care (versus disgruntled/indifferent employees run across at other generic/chain pizza joints). Several employees had asked if I had been helped yet.
-- Quality, sumptuous ingredients make for an impressively weighty pie--i.e. they don't skimp. Kudos to Delish for keeping the prices affordable while still putting out a quality product.
-- Quick, consistently reliable pie within 20 minutes of ordering.
-- Yes, high chairs (the wooden kind, 3 or 4, see picture).
-- Bar height order/payment counter can be a put-off for wheelchair bound patrons.
-- Small dining/waiting/ordering area completely taken up by one side being a long, shared table, and the other side two bar-height tables (see pictures). In a way I feel that this pizza place is a hidden gem.  It's on the other side of the freeway from the school at a part of town that is bordering on sketchy (but not quite there yet). <Review>Forrest R.
8.16.2018

I went online looking for a new pizza establishment and stumbled upon
Delish. I checked their menu out and decided to give them a try. When I called, the staff was very friendly and professional. I ordered a large combo, the price and delivery charge was much lower than I expected, compared to other pizza places in my area.
I received my delivery on time, the delivery person (I forgot her name) was very courteous. They even included condiments, parmesan cheese, peppers, 4 containers of dipping sauce, plates and napkins..which was a nice surprise !!!
As many of you know, when you get your pizza, open it and pull off a slice, the perforated cardboard (where the pizza sits) is usually a total grease bowl, not this place, it was almost grease free !!!. The pizza was excellent, all fresh ingredients  !!!

<pictures>None</pictures><user>115561472282744167640< /user><user_name>Full Bore V8<//user_name>< review>
We experienced this place during happy hour at their rooftop area. The heaters and fireplaces kept us warm and cozy during the cold fall evenings.

Happy hour cocktail selections aren't much but they're all good classic drinks. The food selection for happy hour is superb for the price and perfect for sharing.

Best of all, we had great service from our waiter, Peter. He was very friendly, helpful and accommodating. Hats off to him for serving us. I recommend this place if you're visiting Carmel and want a nice happy hour experience for couples or a small group.

Next time, I'll try the ground floor main dining area for full dinner. I'm sure it will be just as good.<//review>

< review>
The food and drinks were great, as well as the service. I got the sweet potato fries, calamari, and the garlic bread, all of which was delicious.   All of our drinks were expertly made. Oh, and our server, who was probably taking care of 50 people, was super on top of his game!

Downside: My friends and I were on the rooftop patio, which is gorgeous, but it also gets really cold up there once the sun goes down. One of the heaters in our corner wasn't working, leaving half the group shivering. The biggest problem was the wind. I think it would benefit Vesuvio and their guest to add glass panels around the border of the patio to block the wind.</review>

< Text>
Christian and Gian Antonio Pepe are trying hard to make Vesuvio stand out in the high competitive Carmel dining scene, but not everything they're trying works well. Vesuvio's versions of classic Mediterranean dishes, such as grilled artichokes, grilled octopus, and the famous Pepe cannelloni tricolore are sure to please, and the eggplant parmesan is superb. The Italo-Japanese fusion sushi and overly complicated cocktails...not so much. Prices don't provide good value and the service was slower than it should be at this level. Overall, unless the two Pepe sons can level up, Signore Pepe's original Little Napoli will remain a better choice.</Text>

<review>This is a very special place and I mean that most sincerely. Yes the architecture is great the food was great the staff is great the environment is absolutely gorgeous, yes yes yes. Two things I must mention . I realized a day later that I left a purchase behind. I called they had it and were already trying to locate me. Sarah in the Phoenix gift shop was a delight to talk to and even though I offered to pay for shipping she cheerly declined as she wanted it sent out to me at no charge. I was a first-time customer not even a regular and I was so taken aback that she would do this for me. But the very very most special thing about this place is it's ambience number one, no forced piped-in outside music, one was allowed to enjoy the simple experience, The Wonder of being there in peace. Number two, they are very smart and they respect their place, there is no internet for customers to use. Can you imagine what it felt like to look around during a glorious lunch time and not one single person was on a phone? The simple joy of conversation took over. < text>
The rooftop bar at Vesuvio is my favorite place to grab an adult happy meal & cocktail. Easiest one of my top 5 hamburgers! Recommend the truffle fries to go with the burger and aioli.
The restaurant down stairs is good. The pastas are always great, especially the orechiette, and seafood has always been exceptional.The quality of the food can sometimes be inconsistent and is the only reason I'm giving 4 instead of 5 Stars. I've eaten in the main (downstairs) dining room 4 or 5 times and 2 of those times I've ordered a steak (ribeye). Both times the steak was over cooked. Sometimes the sauces (either for pasta, or steak, or on fish) can be oily, but its not the norm.</text>

< review>
We went there late on a Thursday evening. The restaurant was not very full but they sat us in a corner where we felt cramped in with other guests. The table was extremely wobbly and we had to prop it up with our napkin to make it work. The service was unfortunately very slow and indifferent. We ordered garlic bread which did not appear until we reminded the waiter of it. The glass of red wine I ordered at the beginning showed up after the meal was already served. The wild boar bolognese sounded tasty but was a clump of pasta and tasted only so and so. Overall, our visit to the restaurant was quite disappointing and we don't plan to eat here again.<//review>

< text>
For starters, all we got was bread for dipping in oil and balsamic. It was delicious and hot, plus it came in a cute grape shaped container; however we got the bread with our cocktails/beer.. a half hour later.. when the busboy was pouring my water he accidentally spilled water on the table  (fortunately not my lap) he did not come back and wipe our table.
The mr. got a filet for entree and it was cooked to a perfect medium, the broccoli was inedible due to the fact it was over cooked so it was mushy, the mashed potatoes were boxed (I grew up on boxed mashed potatoes) I could feel the flakes on my tongue. They weren't even buttered. :-(
I got the cannelloni tricolore. And it was good, I wish the pesto was more prominent, but i wish had tried something else.. everything just seemed to blend together. I know it was a Saturday and all but I felt like they were rushing us out. Kind of disappointed with the overall experience. We won't be back. I'm glad my green tea cocktail was amazing though.</text>
